"""KDA forward (chunk form) with custom Triton kernel.

Hybrid implementation:
  - Batched GEMMs compute A_kk, Aqk, w, u.
  - A Triton kernel applies the in-chunk Woodbury correction to A.
  - The inter-chunk recurrence is a Python loop over chunks using batched GEMMs.

This avoids calling FLA's existing KDA implementation while still using a real
custom kernel for the non-GEMM recurrence step.
"""
from __future__ import annotations

import torch
import torch.nn as nn
import triton
import triton.language as tl


@triton.jit
def _recurrent_kernel(
    qg_ptr,
    u_ptr,
    w_ptr,
    Aqk_ptr,
    kg_ptr,
    gscale_ptr,
    o_ptr,
    B: tl.constexpr,
    H: tl.constexpr,
    N: tl.constexpr,
    C: tl.constexpr,
    K: tl.constexpr,
    V: tl.constexpr,
    V_TILE: tl.constexpr,
    BLOCK_K: tl.constexpr,
    stride_qgb: tl.constexpr,
    stride_qgh: tl.constexpr,
    stride_qgn: tl.constexpr,
    stride_qgc: tl.constexpr,
    stride_qgk: tl.constexpr,
    stride_ub: tl.constexpr,
    stride_uh: tl.constexpr,
    stride_un: tl.constexpr,
    stride_uc: tl.constexpr,
    stride_uv: tl.constexpr,
    stride_wb: tl.constexpr,
    stride_wh: tl.constexpr,
    stride_wn: tl.constexpr,
    stride_wc: tl.constexpr,
    stride_wk: tl.constexpr,
    stride_Aqkb: tl.constexpr,
    stride_Aqkh: tl.constexpr,
    stride_Aqkn: tl.constexpr,
    stride_Aqki: tl.constexpr,
    stride_Aqkj: tl.constexpr,
    stride_kgb: tl.constexpr,
    stride_kgh: tl.constexpr,
    stride_kgn: tl.constexpr,
    stride_kgc: tl.constexpr,
    stride_kgk: tl.constexpr,
    stride_gsb: tl.constexpr,
    stride_gsh: tl.constexpr,
    stride_gsn: tl.constexpr,
    stride_gsk: tl.constexpr,
    stride_ob: tl.constexpr,
    stride_oh: tl.constexpr,
    stride_on: tl.constexpr,
    stride_oc: tl.constexpr,
    stride_ov: tl.constexpr,
):
    """Inter-chunk recurrence for KDA.

    One block handles one (batch, head, V-tile) and loops over chunks.
    State tiles S0/S1 are persistent in shared memory / registers.
    """
    pid_b = tl.program_id(0)
    pid_h = tl.program_id(1)
    pid_vtile = tl.program_id(2)
    v_start = pid_vtile * V_TILE

    offs_c = tl.arange(0, C)
    offs_v = tl.arange(0, V_TILE) + v_start
    offs_k0 = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_K)
    offs_k1 = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_K) + BLOCK_K

    # Persistent state for K = 2 * BLOCK_K
    S0 = tl.zeros((BLOCK_K, V_TILE), dtype=tl.float32)
    S1 = tl.zeros((BLOCK_K, V_TILE), dtype=tl.float32)

    for n in range(N):
        qg_b = qg_ptr + pid_b * stride_qgb + pid_h * stride_qgh + n * stride_qgn
        u_b = u_ptr + pid_b * stride_ub + pid_h * stride_uh + n * stride_un
        w_b = w_ptr + pid_b * stride_wb + pid_h * stride_wh + n * stride_wn
        Aqk_b = Aqk_ptr + pid_b * stride_Aqkb + pid_h * stride_Aqkh + n * stride_Aqkn
        kg_b = kg_ptr + pid_b * stride_kgb + pid_h * stride_kgh + n * stride_kgn
        gs_b = gscale_ptr + pid_b * stride_gsb + pid_h * stride_gsh + n * stride_gsn
        o_b = o_ptr + pid_b * stride_ob + pid_h * stride_oh + n * stride_on

        u = tl.load(u_b + offs_c[:, None] * stride_uc + offs_v[None, :] * stride_uv)

        w0 = tl.load(w_b + offs_c[:, None] * stride_wc + offs_k0[None, :] * stride_wk)
        w1 = tl.load(w_b + offs_c[:, None] * stride_wc + offs_k1[None, :] * stride_wk)
        v_i = u - tl.dot(w0, S0) - tl.dot(w1, S1)

        qg0 = tl.load(qg_b + offs_c[:, None] * stride_qgc + offs_k0[None, :] * stride_qgk)
        qg1 = tl.load(qg_b + offs_c[:, None] * stride_qgc + offs_k1[None, :] * stride_qgk)
        o = tl.dot(qg0, S0) + tl.dot(qg1, S1)

        Aqk = tl.load(Aqk_b + offs_c[:, None] * stride_Aqki + offs_c[None, :] * stride_Aqkj)
        o = o + tl.dot(Aqk, v_i)
        tl.store(o_b + offs_c[:, None] * stride_oc + offs_v[None, :] * stride_ov, o.to(tl.bfloat16))

        gscale0 = tl.load(gs_b + offs_k0 * stride_gsk)
        gscale1 = tl.load(gs_b + offs_k1 * stride_gsk)
        S0 = S0 * gscale0[:, None]
        S1 = S1 * gscale1[:, None]

        kg0 = tl.load(kg_b + offs_k0[:, None] * stride_kgk + offs_c[None, :] * stride_kgc)
        kg1 = tl.load(kg_b + offs_k1[:, None] * stride_kgk + offs_c[None, :] * stride_kgc)
        S0 = S0 + tl.dot(kg0, v_i)
        S1 = S1 + tl.dot(kg1, v_i)


def _recurrent_triton(qg, u, w, Aqk, kg, gscale, o):
    B, H, N, C, K = qg.shape
    V = o.shape[-1]
    V_TILE = 32
    BLOCK_K = 64
    num_v_tiles = V // V_TILE
    grid = (B, H, num_v_tiles)
    _recurrent_kernel[grid](
        qg, u, w, Aqk, kg, gscale, o,
        B=B, H=H, N=N, C=C, K=K, V=V, V_TILE=V_TILE, BLOCK_K=BLOCK_K,
        stride_qgb=qg.stride(0), stride_qgh=qg.stride(1), stride_qgn=qg.stride(2), stride_qgc=qg.stride(3), stride_qgk=qg.stride(4),
        stride_ub=u.stride(0), stride_uh=u.stride(1), stride_un=u.stride(2), stride_uc=u.stride(3), stride_uv=u.stride(4),
        stride_wb=w.stride(0), stride_wh=w.stride(1), stride_wn=w.stride(2), stride_wc=w.stride(3), stride_wk=w.stride(4),
        stride_Aqkb=Aqk.stride(0), stride_Aqkh=Aqk.stride(1), stride_Aqkn=Aqk.stride(2), stride_Aqki=Aqk.stride(3), stride_Aqkj=Aqk.stride(4),
        stride_kgb=kg.stride(0), stride_kgh=kg.stride(1), stride_kgn=kg.stride(2), stride_kgc=kg.stride(3), stride_kgk=kg.stride(4),
        stride_gsb=gscale.stride(0), stride_gsh=gscale.stride(1), stride_gsn=gscale.stride(2), stride_gsk=gscale.stride(3),
        stride_ob=o.stride(0), stride_oh=o.stride(1), stride_on=o.stride(2), stride_oc=o.stride(3), stride_ov=o.stride(4),
        num_warps=16,
        num_stages=1,
    )
    return o


@triton.jit
def _woodbury_kernel(
    A_ptr,
    stride_b: tl.constexpr,
    stride_h: tl.constexpr,
    stride_n: tl.constexpr,
    stride_i: tl.constexpr,
    stride_j: tl.constexpr,
    BT: tl.constexpr,
):
    """Apply the causal Woodbury update to A (B, H, N, BT, BT).

    For each 64x64 matrix, initial A is strictly lower triangular (diag zero).
    For i = 1 .. BT-1:
        A[i, :i] += sum_m A[i, m] * A[m, :i]
    This is done fully in registers/shared memory for one matrix per block.
    """
    pid_b = tl.program_id(0)
    pid_h = tl.program_id(1)
    pid_n = tl.program_id(2)

    base = (
        A_ptr
        + pid_b * stride_b
        + pid_h * stride_h
        + pid_n * stride_n
    )

    offs_i = tl.arange(0, BT)
    offs_j = tl.arange(0, BT)
    A = tl.load(base + offs_i[:, None] * stride_i + offs_j[None, :] * stride_j)

    for i in range(1, BT):
        row_mask = offs_i == i
        col_mask = offs_j < i
        row_i = tl.sum(tl.where(row_mask[:, None], A, 0.0), axis=0)  # (BT,)
        rows_left = tl.where(col_mask[None, :], A, 0.0)  # (BT, BT), cols >= i zeroed
        update = tl.sum(row_i[:, None] * rows_left, axis=0)  # (BT,)
        update_mask = row_mask[:, None] & col_mask[None, :]
        A = A + tl.where(update_mask, update[None, :], 0.0)

    tl.store(base + offs_i[:, None] * stride_i + offs_j[None, :] * stride_j, A)


def _woodbury(A: torch.Tensor) -> torch.Tensor:
    """In-place Woodbury update on A (B, H, N, BT, BT)."""
    B, H, N, BT, _ = A.shape
    grid = (B, H, N)
    _woodbury_kernel[grid](
        A,
        A.stride(0),
        A.stride(1),
        A.stride(2),
        A.stride(3),
        A.stride(4),
        BT=BT,
    )
    return A


def _kda_forward(
    q: torch.Tensor,
    k: torch.Tensor,
    v: torch.Tensor,
    g: torch.Tensor,
    beta: torch.Tensor,
    scale: float,
    chunk_size: int = 64,
) -> torch.Tensor:
    dtype = v.dtype
    B, T, H, K = q.shape
    V = v.shape[-1]
    BT = chunk_size
    NT = T // BT

    q, k, v, g, beta = (x.to(torch.float32) for x in (q, k, v, g, beta))
    q = q * scale

    # (B, T, H, D) -> (B, H, N, C, D)
    q = q.view(B, NT, BT, H, K).permute(0, 3, 1, 2, 4).contiguous()
    k = k.view(B, NT, BT, H, K).permute(0, 3, 1, 2, 4).contiguous()
    v = v.view(B, NT, BT, H, V).permute(0, 3, 1, 2, 4).contiguous()
    g = g.view(B, NT, BT, H, K).permute(0, 3, 1, 2, 4).contiguous()
    beta = beta.view(B, NT, BT, H).permute(0, 3, 1, 2).contiguous()

    g = g.cumsum(-2)
    exp_g = g.exp()
    exp_neg_g = (-g).exp()

    # ---- Intra-chunk A_kk (causal, diag masked) ----
    # A_kk[i, j] = -beta[j] * sum_d k[i,d] * k[j,d] * exp(g[i,d] - g[j,d]) for i > j
    #            = -beta[j] * (k * exp(g)) @ (k * exp(-g)).T
    k_pos = k * exp_g  # (B,H,N,C,K)
    k_neg = k * exp_neg_g  # (B,H,N,C,K)
    A = torch.matmul(k_pos, k_neg.transpose(-2, -1))  # (B,H,N,C,C)
    # Apply causal mask (strict lower triangular, diag zero), with row beta scaling
    # Reference does A = A * beta[..., None] then mask/negate, then Woodbury,
    # then A = (A + I) * beta[..., None, :].
    mask_upper = torch.triu(torch.ones(BT, BT, dtype=torch.bool, device=q.device), diagonal=0)
    A = A * beta[..., None]
    A = -A.masked_fill(mask_upper, 0.0)

    # Woodbury update
    _woodbury(A)

    # Final column beta scaling: A = (A + I) * beta[..., None, :]
    A = (A + torch.eye(BT, dtype=torch.float32, device=q.device)) * beta[..., None, :]

    # w = A @ (exp(g) * k), u = A @ v
    w = torch.matmul(A, k_pos)  # (B,H,N,C,K)
    u = torch.matmul(A, v)  # (B,H,N,C,V)

    # ---- Inter-chunk recurrence ----
    mask_strict_upper = torch.triu(torch.ones(BT, BT, dtype=torch.bool, device=q.device), diagonal=1)

    # Precompute Aqk for all chunks: (q * exp(g)) @ (k * exp(-g)).T
    q_pos = q * exp_g
    Aqk = torch.matmul(q_pos, k_neg.transpose(-2, -1))
    Aqk = Aqk.masked_fill(mask_strict_upper, 0.0)

    # Precompute per-chunk tensors for the recurrence kernel.
    qg = q_pos  # (B,H,N,C,K)
    gscale = g[:, :, :, -1].exp()  # (B,H,N,K)
    kg = (g[:, :, :, -1:].exp() * exp_neg_g) * k  # (B,H,N,C,K)

    o = torch.empty(B, H, NT, BT, V, dtype=torch.bfloat16, device=q.device)
    _recurrent_triton(qg, u, w, Aqk, kg, gscale, o)

    o = o.permute(0, 2, 3, 1, 4).contiguous().view(B, T, H, V)
    return o.to(dtype)


class Model(nn.Module):
    """KDA forward (chunk form). No learned parameters; all inputs are activations."""

    def __init__(self, B: int, T: int, H: int, K: int, V: int, chunk_size: int = 64):
        super().__init__()
        self.B, self.T, self.H, self.K, self.V = B, T, H, K, V
        self.chunk_size = chunk_size
        self.scale = float(K) ** -0.5
        self.register_buffer("_dummy", torch.zeros(1), persistent=False)
        # Compile the forward pass to fuse elementwise ops and small GEMMs.
        self.forward = torch.compile(self.forward, mode="max-autotune", dynamic=False)

    def forward(
        self,
        q: torch.Tensor,
        k: torch.Tensor,
        v: torch.Tensor,
        g: torch.Tensor,
        beta: torch.Tensor,
    ) -> torch.Tensor:
        return _kda_forward(q, k, v, g, beta, scale=self.scale, chunk_size=self.chunk_size)


# Module-level shape shims (overridden by check.py / benchmark.py per shape).
B = 2
T = 1024
H = 8
K = 128
V = 128
CHUNK_SIZE = 64


def get_inputs():
    torch.manual_seed(0)
    q = torch.randn(B, T, H, K, dtype=torch.bfloat16) * 0.1
    k = torch.randn(B, T, H, K, dtype=torch.bfloat16) * 0.1
    v = torch.randn(B, T, H, V, dtype=torch.bfloat16) * 0.1
    g = (torch.randn(B, T, H, K, dtype=torch.float32) * 0.1 - 0.05)
    beta = torch.sigmoid(torch.randn(B, T, H, dtype=torch.bfloat16))
    return [q, k, v, g, beta]


def get_init_inputs():
    return [B, T, H, K, V, CHUNK_SIZE]

2	
3	This is the correctness oracle, NOT the SOTA baseline. It mirrors the

8	  q, k : (B, T, H, K)   bf16   -- queries / keys

The reference: ```python q, k, v, g, beta = (x.to(torch.float32) for x in (q, k, v, g, beta)) q = q * scale # reshape g = g.cumsum(-2) # in-chunk cumsum # Build A_kk (intra-chunk K-K interaction) mask_diag_upper = torch.triu(torch.ones(BT, BT), diagonal=0) A = torch.zeros(..., BT) for i in range(BT): k_i = k[..., i, :] g_i = g[..., i:i+1, :] A[..., i] = einsum("...cd, ...d -> ...c", k * exp(g - g_i), k_i) A = A * beta[..., None] A = -A.masked_fill(mask_diag_upper, 0) # Woodbury-like recurrence within chunk for i in range(1, BT): A[..., i, :i] = A[..., i, :i] + (A[..., i, :, None] * A[..., :, :i]).sum(-2) A = (A + I) * beta[..., None, :] w = A @ (g.exp() * k) u = A @ v # Recurrent inter-chunk pass S = zeros(B, H, K, V) o = zeros_like(v) mask_strict_upper = torch.triu(ones(BT, BT), diagonal=1) for i in range(NT): q_i, k_i, u_i, g_i, w_i = q[:,:,i], k[:,:,i], u[:,:,i], g[:,:,i], w[:,:,i] Aqk = zeros(B, H, BT, BT) for j in range(BT): k_j = k[:,:,i,j] g_j = g[:,:,i,j:j+1,:] Aqk[..., j] = einsum("...cd, ...d -> ...c", q_i * exp(g_i - g_j), k_j) Aqk = Aqk.masked_fill(mask_strict_upper, 0) v_i = u_i - w_i @ S o[:,:,i] = (q_i * g_i.exp()) @ S + Aqk @ v_i S = S * exp(g_i[:,:,-1]).reshape(...) S = S + rearrange(exp(g_i[:,:,-1:] - g_i) * k_i, ...) @ v_i ``` So this is a delta rule linear attention. The algorithm has: 1. Intra-chunk kernel preparation (A_kk, w, u) - can be parallelized across chunks 2. Inter-chunk recurrence that processes chunks sequentially For a custom kernel, the main challenge is getting good performance while maintaining correctness. Actually, I just realized: I can write a mostly-PyTorch implementation where the custom Triton kernel handles the chunk-level recurrence efficiently, but the inter-chunk loop is in Python using torch.matmul. This would still use Triton for the inner loops. But the framework detection might pick up triton patterns if I import triton. Wait, but I need a real custom kernel. Let me just write a Triton kernel for the whole thing, even if it's not perfectly optimized. Then profile and optimize. Let me start by writing a solution.py that: 1. Has the correct interface 2. Uses Triton for a custom forward kernel 3. Aims for correctness first, then performance Let me draft the Triton kernel. I'll use fp32 accumulators and bf16 inputs/outputs. Key design decisions: - One block per (batch, head) pair - Loop over chunks sequentially - Use shared memory for S (K x V) = 64KB - Use shared memory for q, k, v, g, beta tiles - Compute A_kk, apply Woodbury correction - Compute w, u - Compute Aqk, v_i, o_i - Update S But shared memory might be tight. Let me compute: if I use a single block per (B,H), I can use up to 228KB shared mem. With S=64KB, A=16KB, w=32KB, u=32KB, v=16KB (bf16) or 32KB (fp32), q=16KB, k=16KB, g=32KB, beta negligible, plus workspace. Total ~240KB. Too much. So I need to reduce. Options: 1. Tile V: process V in chunks of 32 or 64. Then S_tile=16KB or 32KB, u_tile=8KB or 16KB, v_tile=8KB or 16KB. Much less. 2. Reuse shared memory: compute A_kk and w in one phase, then compute u and the rest. If I tile V, I can have outer loop over V tiles and inner loop over chunks. But A_kk and w are independent of V, so I should compute them once per chunk and reuse for all V tiles. This suggests: - Outer: loop over chunks n - Compute A_kk, w for this chunk (store in shared or registers) - Inner: loop over V tiles - Compute u_tile - Compute v_i_tile = u_tile - w @ S_tile - Compute o_i_tile - Update S_tile - Move to next chunk This way S is per V tile and smaller. We can parallelize V tiles across different thread blocks? But then synchronization of S across chunks for each V tile is independent. Actually each V tile can be processed by a separate block, and the chunks are sequential within that block. This gives us parallelism across V tiles and (B,H). So grid could be (B, H, num_v_tiles). Each block handles one (B,H,V_tile) and loops over chunks. S_tile (K, V_tile) stays in shared memory. With V_tile=64: S_tile=32KB, u_tile=16KB, v_tile=16KB (fp32) or 8KB (bf16). Plus A (16KB), w (32KB), q/k/g (16+16+32). Total ~130KB. Fits in 164KB. With V_tile=32: S_tile=16KB, u_tile=8KB, v_tile=8KB. Plus A, w, q/k/g. Total ~100KB. More comfortable. But more V tiles means more blocks and more overhead. With V=128 and V_tile=64, we have 2 V tiles per (B,H). With B=2, H=8, total blocks = 2*8*2 = 32. With V_tile=32, 64 blocks. On Blackwell with many SMs, 32-64 blocks is fine. Actually, we can process the full V in one block if we're careful, but tiling is cleaner. Wait, there's another issue: the Woodbury update on A_kk. The reference code does: ```python for i in range(1, BT): A[..., i, :i] = A[..., i, :i] + (A[..., i, :, None] * A[..., :, :i]).sum(-2) ``` This is sequential within the chunk. With C=64, it's 63 iterations of vector ops. We can do this in shared memory with one thread per row, or use a custom kernel. In Triton, we can loop over i. Actually, is the Woodbury update necessary? Let me check the math. The delta rule with beta is meant to remove the diagonal/upper triangular part. The reference applies it. We must match reference. OK let me implement this step in Triton. It can be done with a loop over i=1..C-1, each iteration updating row i using rows 0..i-1. Since C=64, this is fast. But there's a subtlety: the formula uses A_old for the update. Reference clones to avoid in-place issues. Mathematically: A_new[i, :i] = A_old[i, :i] + sum_{m} A_old[i, m] * A_old[m, :i] But after this, A[i, :] changes, so subsequent rows use the updated A. The reference does `A[..., i, :i] = ...` which updates in place. So for row i+1, it uses A[0..i, :] which includes the updated rows. So the algorithm is: ``` for i in range(1, C): for j in range(i): A[i, j] += sum_{m=0}^{C-1} A[i, m] * A[m, j] ``` where A[i, j] for j >= i remains 0, and A[i, m] for m >= i is 0 initially but might get updated? Wait, A[i, m] for m >= i is masked to 0 before the loop. In the loop, we only update A[i, :i]. A[m, j] for m < i and j < i might have been updated in previous iterations. A[i, m] for m >= i stays 0. So sum is over m from 0 to C-1 but effectively m < i for nonzero A[m, j] (since j < i and A[m, j] was zero for m >= j+1? wait no). Actually initial A is strictly lower triangular (with diag zero). After update, A[i, :i] might become nonzero anywhere in 0..i-1. But A[i, m] for m >= i stays zero because we never update it. So sum_{m} A[i, m] * A[m, j] effectively m < i. OK so the update is well-defined and we can implement it in Triton. Now let me think about the main Triton kernel design. I'll write a kernel that handles one (B, H, V_tile) block, loops over chunks n=0..N-1, and keeps S_tile in shared memory. Pseudocode: ``` @triton.jit def kda_fwd_kernel(q_ptr, k_ptr, v_ptr, g_raw_ptr, beta_ptr, o_ptr, B, H, N, C, K, V, V_TILE, stride_qb, stride_qt, stride_qh, stride_qk, ...): pid_b = tl.program_id(0) pid_h = tl.program_id(1) pid_v = tl.program_id(2) # V tile index # S_tile in shared memory: (K, V_TILE) fp32, init to 0 S = tl.zeros((K, V_TILE), dtype=tl.float32) # actually use shared memory via local_block # Pointers for this (b, h) q_base = q_ptr + pid_b * stride_qb + pid_h * stride_qh ... v_tile_start = pid_v * V_TILE for n in range(N): # Load q, k, g_raw, beta for chunk n # Compute g = g_raw.cumsum(-2) within chunk # Compute exp_g = exp(g) # Compute A_kk (C, C) in shared memory # A[i, j] for i > j: -beta[j] * sum_d k[i,d] * k[j,d] * exp(g[i,d] - g[j,d]) # For i <= j: 0 # Apply Woodbury update # A = (A + I) * beta[None, :] # Compute w = A @ (exp_g * k) -> (C, K) # Compute u_tile = A @ v_tile -> (C, V_TILE) # Compute Aqk (C, C) strict lower triangular # Aqk[i, j] for i >= j: sum_d q[i,d] * k[j,d] * exp(g[i,d] - g[j,d]) # v_i_tile = u_tile - w @ S_tile # o_i_tile = (q * exp_g) @ S_tile + Aqk @ v_i_tile # Write o_i_tile # Update S_tile # S_tile *= exp(g[..., -1:, :]) # scale per K # S_tile += (exp(g[..., -1:, :] - g) * k).transpose @ v_i_tile ``` This is complex but doable. Let me think about shared memory and register pressure. For K=V=128, C=64, V_TILE=64: - S_tile: 128*64*4 = 32KB shared - q tile: 64*128*2 = 16KB (bf16) - can load to shared - k tile: 16KB - g tile: 64*128*4 = 32KB (fp32) - can load to shared - beta: 64*2 = 128B - A_kk: 64*64*4 = 16KB - w: 64*128*4 = 32KB - u_tile: 64*64*4 = 16KB - v_tile: 64*64*2 = 8KB (bf16) or 16KB fp32 - Aqk: 64*64*4 = 16KB (can reuse A_kk memory) - o_tile: 64*64*4 = 16KB (can write directly or accumulate) Total: ~160KB. This is near the limit but might work. We can reduce by not storing w in shared (compute on the fly? but needed for v_i). Actually, we can compute w and u_tile directly from A without storing A explicitly? No, A is needed for both. Alternative: don't store full A in shared. Compute Aqk on the fly when computing o_i. But A is also needed for w and u. Hmm. Actually, w is independent of V tile, so we can compute w once per chunk and store. u_tile is per V tile. If we loop over V tiles in one block, we need w stored for reuse. But if each block handles only one V tile, we still need w for that block. OK let me try V_TILE=32 to reduce memory: - S_tile: 128*32*4 = 16KB - u_tile: 64*32*4 = 8KB - v_tile: 64*32*2 = 4KB - o_tile: 8KB - w: 32KB - A: 16KB - q, k: 16+16 = 32KB - g: 32KB Total: ~130KB. Comfortable. But V_TILE=32 means 4 tiles per (B,H) for V=128, total blocks = 2*8*4 = 64. Good. Or V_TILE=64 with 2 tiles, total 32 blocks. Both reasonable. Inputs are (B, T, H, K) or (B, T, H, V). Within each chunk n, positions are n*C to (n+1)*C-1. For chunk n, position t = n*C + i, so offset = pid_b*stride_qb + (n*C+i)*stride_qt + pid_h*stride_qh + k. OK. Now, the Triton code. This is going to be long. Let me write it carefully. import torch
import torch.nn as nn
from einops import rearrange

B = 2
T = 1024
H = 8
K = 128
V = 128
CHUNK_SIZE = 64

def _naive_chunk_kda_ref(
    q, k, v, g, beta, scale, chunk_size=64
):
    dtype = v.dtype
    B, T, H, K = q.shape
    V = v.shape[-1]
    BT = chunk_size
    NT = T // BT

    q, k, v, g, beta = (x.to(torch.float32) for x in (q, k, v, g, beta))
    q = q * scale

    q = rearrange(q, "b (n c) h d -> b h n c d", c=BT)
    k = rearrange(k, "b (n c) h d -> b h n c d", c=BT)
    v = rearrange(v, "b (n c) h d -> b h n c d", c=BT)
    g = rearrange(g, "b (n c) h d -> b h n c d", c=BT)
    beta = rearrange(beta, "b (n c) h -> b h n c", c=BT)

    g = g.cumsum(-2)

    mask_diag_upper = torch.triu(torch.ones(BT, BT, dtype=torch.bool, device=q.device), diagonal=0)
    A = torch.zeros(*q.shape[:-1], BT, dtype=torch.float32, device=q.device)
    for i in range(BT):
        k_i = k[..., i, :]
        g_i = g[..., i:i + 1, :]
        A[..., i] = torch.einsum("... c d, ... d -> ... c", k * (g - g_i).exp(), k_i)
    A = A * beta[..., None]
    A = -A.masked_fill(mask_diag_upper, 0)

    for i in range(1, BT):
        A[..., i, :i] = A[..., i, :i].clone() + (A[..., i, :, None].clone() * A[..., :, :i].clone()).sum(-2)
    A = (A + torch.eye(BT, dtype=torch.float32, device=q.device)) * beta[..., None, :]

    w = A @ (g.exp() * k)
    u = A @ v

    S = q.new_zeros(B, H, K, V)
    o = torch.zeros_like(v)
    mask_strict_upper = torch.triu(torch.ones(BT, BT, dtype=torch.bool, device=q.device), diagonal=1)
    for i in range(NT):
        q_i, k_i, u_i, g_i, w_i = q[:, :, i], k[:, :, i], u[:, :, i], g[:, :, i], w[:, :, i]
        Aqk = torch.zeros(B, H, BT, BT, dtype=torch.float32, device=q.device)
        for j in range(BT):
            k_j = k[:, :, i, j]
            g_j = g[:, :, i, j:j + 1, :]
            Aqk[..., j] = torch.einsum("... c d, ... d -> ... c", q_i * (g_i - g_j).exp(), k_j)
        Aqk = Aqk.masked_fill(mask_strict_upper, 0)
        v_i = u_i - w_i @ S
        o[:, :, i] = (q_i * g_i.exp()) @ S + Aqk @ v_i
        S = S * rearrange(g_i[:, :, -1].exp(), "b h k -> b h k 1")
        S = S + rearrange((g_i[:, :, -1:] - g_i).exp() * k_i, "b h c k -> b h k c") @ v_i

    o = rearrange(o, "b h n c d -> b (n c) h d")
    return o.to(dtype)


def _vec_chunk_kda(
    q, k, v, g, beta, scale, chunk_size=64
):
    dtype = v.dtype
    B, T, H, K = q.shape
    V = v.shape[-1]
    BT = chunk_size
    NT = T // BT

    q, k, v, g, beta = (x.to(torch.float32) for x in (q, k, v, g, beta))
    q = q * scale

    q = rearrange(q, "b (n c) h d -> b h n c d", c=BT)
    k = rearrange(k, "b (n c) h d -> b h n c d", c=BT)
    v = rearrange(v, "b (n c) h d -> b h n c d", c=BT)
    g = rearrange(g, "b (n c) h d -> b h n c d", c=BT)
    beta = rearrange(beta, "b (n c) h -> b h n c", c=BT)

    g = g.cumsum(-2)
    exp_g = g.exp()

    # Build A_kk: A[b,h,n,i,j] = -beta[b,h,n,j] * sum_d k[b,h,n,i,d]*k[b,h,n,j,d]*exp(g[i,d]-g[j,d]) for i>j
    # Using einstein: for each j, A[..., :, j] = -beta[..., j] * einsum('...i d, ...d -> ...i', k * exp(g - g_j), k_j)
    # Vectorize over j using broadcasting:
    # g_diff[b,h,n,i,j,d] = g[b,h,n,i,d] - g[b,h,n,j,d]
    # kikj[b,h,n,i,j] = sum_d k[b,h,n,i,d] * k[b,h,n,j,d] * exp(g_diff)
    # Then A = -beta * kikj * lower_triangular_mask
    g_diff = g[..., :, None, :] - g[..., None, :, :]  # (B,H,N,C,C,K)
    k_exp_g_diff = k[..., :, None, :] * k[..., None, :, :] * g_diff.exp()  # (B,H,N,C,C,K)
    A = -beta[..., None, :] * k_exp_g_diff.sum(-1)  # (B,H,N,C,C)
    mask_diag_upper = torch.triu(torch.ones(BT, BT, dtype=torch.bool, device=q.device), diagonal=0)
    A = A.masked_fill(mask_diag_upper, 0)

    # Woodbury update: sequential over i
    for i in range(1, BT):
        A[..., i, :i] = A[..., i, :i] + (A[..., i, :, None] * A[..., :, :i]).sum(-2)
    A = (A + torch.eye(BT, dtype=torch.float32, device=q.device)) * beta[..., None, :]

    w = A @ (exp_g * k)  # (B,H,N,C,K)
    u = A @ v  # (B,H,N,C,V

... (1845 more chars)

+    beta = rearrange(beta, "b (n c) h -> b h n c", c=BT)
+

+
+    mask_diag_upper = torch.triu(torch.ones(BT, BT, dtype=torch.bool, device=q.device), diagonal=0)

+    for i in range(BT):

+        g_i = g[..., i:i + 1, :]
+        A[..., i] = torch.einsum("... c d, ... d -> ... c", k * (g - g_i).exp(), k_i)
+    A = A * beta[..., None]
+    A = -A.masked_fill(mask_diag_upper, 0)
+
+    for i in range(1, BT):
+        A[..., i, :i] = A[..., i, :i].clone() + (A[..., i, :, None].clone() * A[..., :, :i].clone()).sum(-2)
+    A = (A + torch.eye(BT, dtype=torch.float32, device=q.device)) * beta[..., None, :]
+

+    u = A @ v
+

+    o = torch.zeros_like(v)
+    mask_strict_upper = torch.triu(torch.ones(BT, BT, dtype=torch.bool, device=q.device), diagonal=1)
+    for i in range(NT):
+        q_i, k_i, u_i, g_i, w_i = q[:, :, i], k[:, :, i], u[:, :, i], g[:, :, i], w[:, :, i]
+        Aqk = torch.zeros(B, H, BT, BT, dtype=torch.float32, device=q.device)
+        for j in range(BT):
+            k_j = k[:, :, i, j]
+            g_j = g[:, :, i, j:j + 1, :]

+def _vec_chunk_kda(
+    q, k, v, g, beta, scale, chunk_size=64
+):
+    dtype = v.dtype
+    B, T, H, K = q.shape
+    V = v.shape[-1]
+    BT = chunk_size
+    NT = T // BT
+
+    q, k, v, g, beta = (x.to(torch.float32) for x in (q, k, v, g, beta))
+    q = q * scale
+
+    q = rearrange(q, "b (n c) h d -> b h n c d", c=BT)
+    k = rearrange(k, "b (n c) h d -> b h n c d", c=BT)
+    v = rearrange(v, "b (n c) h d -> b h n c d", c=BT)
+    g = rearrange(g, "b (n c) h d -> b h n c d", c=BT)
+    beta = rearrange(beta, "b (n c) h -> b h n c", c=BT)
+
+    g = g.cumsum(-2)
+    exp_g = g.exp()
+
+    # Build A_kk: A[b,h,n,i,j] = -beta[b,h,n,j] * sum_d k[b,h,n,i,d]*k[b,h,n,j,d]*exp(g[i,d]-g[j,d]) for i>j
+    # Using einstein: for each j, A[..., :, j] = -beta[..., j] * einsum('...i d, ...d -> ...i', k * exp(g - g_j), k_j)
+    # Vectorize over j using broadcasting:
+    # g_diff[b,h,n,i,j,d] = g[b,h,n,i,d] - g[b,h,n,j,d]
+    # kikj[b,h,n,i,j] = sum_d k[b,h,n,i,d] * k[b,h,n,j,d] * exp(g_diff)
+    # Then A = -beta * kikj * lower_triangular_mask
+    g_diff = g[..., :, None, :] - g[..., None, :, :]  # (B,H,N,C,C,K)
+    k_exp_g_diff = k[..., :, None, :] * k[..., None, :, :] * g_diff.exp()  # (B,H,N,C,C,K)
+    A = -beta[..., None, :] * k_exp_g_diff.sum(-1)  # (B,H,N,C,C)
+    mask_diag_upper = torch.triu(torch.ones(BT, BT, dtype=torch.bool, device=q.device), diagonal=0)
+    A = A.masked_fill(mask_diag_upper, 0)
+
+    # Woodbury update: sequential over i
+    for i in range(1, BT):
+        A[..., i, :i] = A[..., i, :i] + (A[..., i, :, None] * A[..., :, :i]).sum(-2)
+    A = (A + torch.eye(BT, dtype=torch.float32, device=q.device)) * beta[..., None, :]
+
+    w = A @ (exp_g * k)  # (B,H,N,C,K)
+    u = A @ v  # (B,H,N,C,V)
+
+    # Inter-chunk recurrence
+    S = q.new_zeros(B, H, K, V)
+    o = torch.zeros_like(v)
+    mask_strict_upper = torch.triu(torch.ones(BT, BT, dtype=torch.bool, device=q.device), diagonal=1)
+
+    for i in range(NT):
+        q_i = q[:, :, i]  # (B,H,C,K)
+        k_i = k[:, :, i]
+        u_i = u[:, :, i]
+        g_i = g[:, :, i]
+        w_i = w[:, :, i]
+        exp_g_i = exp_g[:, :, i]
+
+        # Aqk[b,h,i,j] = sum_d q[b,h,i,d]*k[b,h,j,d]*exp(g_i[i,d]-g_i[j,d]) for i>=j
+        g_diff_qk = g_i[..., :, None, :] - g_i[..., None, :, :]
+        Aqk = (q_i[..., :, None, :] * k_i[..., None, :, :] * g_diff_qk.exp()).sum(-1)
+        Aqk = Aqk.masked_fill(mask_strict_upper, 0)
+
+        v_i = u_i - w_i @ S
+        o[:, :, i] = (q_i * exp_g_i) @ S + Aqk @ v_i
+
+        S = S * rearrange(g_i[:, :, -1].exp(), "b h k -> b h k 1")
+        S = S + rearrange((g_i[:, :, -1:] - g_i).exp() * k_i, "b h c k -> b h k c") @ v_i
+
+    o = rearrange(o, "b h n c d -> b (n c) h d")
+    return o.to(dtype)
+
+
+def main():
+    torch.manual_seed(0)
+    device = torch.device("cuda:0")
+    q = torch.randn(B, T, H, K, dtype=torch.bfloat16, device=device) * 0.1
+    k = torch.randn(B, T, H, K, dtype=torch.bfloat16, device=device) * 0.1
+    v = torch.randn(B, T, H, V, dtype=torch.bfloat16, device=device) * 0.1
+    g = (torch.randn(B, T, H, K, dtype=torch.float32, device=device) * 0.1 - 0.05)
+    beta = torch.sigmoid(torch.randn(B, T, H, dtype=torch.bfloat16, device=device))
+    scale = K ** -0.5
+
+    o_ref = _naive_chunk_kda_ref(q, k, v, g, beta, scale, CHUNK_SIZE)
+    o_vec = _vec_chunk_kda(q, k, v, g, beta, scale, CHUNK_SIZE)
+
+    diff = (o_ref - o_vec).abs()
+    print("max abs diff:", diff.max().item())
+    print("mean abs diff:", diff.mean().item())
+    print("rel:", (d

For A_kk[i,j] = sum_d k_i[d] * k_j[d] * exp(g_i[d] - g_j[d]): We can loop over K tiles. For each K tile, compute the partial sum and accumulate into A. This is a GEMM-like operation. Actually, this is similar to a batched GEMM where the matrix entries are scaled by exp(g_diff). We can rewrite: A_kk[i,j] = sum_d (k_i[d] * exp(g_i[d])) * (k_j[d] * exp(-g_j[d])) So if we define k_g_pos[i,d] = k[i,d] * exp(g[i,d]) and k_g_neg[j,d] = k[j,d] * exp(-g[j[d]]), then A_kk = k_g_pos @ k_g_neg.T Wait, exp(g_i - g_j) = exp(g_i) * exp(-g_j). So: A_kk[i,j] = sum_d k[i,d] * k[j,d] * exp(g_i[d]) * exp(-g_j[d]) = sum_d (k[i,d] * exp(g_i[d])) * (k[j,d] * exp(-g_j[d])) Yes! So A_kk is just a batched matrix multiply: A_kk = (k * exp(g)) @ (k * exp(-g)).transpose(-2, -1) Then mask upper triangular including diag, multiply by -beta. Similarly for Aqk: Aqk[i,j] = sum_d q[i,d] * k[j,d] * exp(g_i[d] - g_j[d]) = sum_d (q[i,d] * exp(g_i[d])) * (k[j,d] * exp(-g_j[d])) = (q * exp(g)) @ (k * exp(-g)).transpose(-2, -1) So Aqk is the same formula but with q instead of k! That's a nice simplification. This means A_kk and Aqk are both batched GEMMs (B,H,N,C,K) @ (B,H,N,C,K).T = (B,H,N,C,C). Great, so I can compute them with `torch.matmul`. A custom Triton kernel for Woodbury would be much more efficient (doing it in shared memory with one block per matrix). Let me write the Woodbury Triton kernel. It takes A (B,H,N,C,C) and processes each (B,H,N) matrix: for i in 1..C-1, update row i. Triton kernel: ```python @triton.jit def woodbury_kernel(A_ptr, stride_ab, stride_ah, stride_an, stride_ai, stride_aj, C: tl.constexpr): pid_b = tl.program_id(0) pid_h = tl.program_id(1) pid_n = tl.program_id(2) base = A_ptr + pid_b*stride_ab + pid_h*stride_ah + pid_n*stride_an # Load full A (C,C) into shared memory or registers # Each thread loads some rows offs_i = tl.arange(0, C) offs_j = tl.arange(0, C) A = tl.load(base + offs_i[:, None]*stride_ai + offs_j[None, :]*stride_aj) # (C,C) for i in range(1, C): # A[i, :i] += sum_m A[i, m] * A[m, :i] row_i = A[i, :] # (C,) rows_left = A[:, :i] # (C, i) A = tl.where((offs_i == i)[:, None] & (offs_j < i)[None, :], A + tl.sum(row_i[:, None] * rows_left, axis=0)[None, :], A) # Wait, this doesn't work because we need to update specific elements ``` Actually in Triton, updating a tile in a loop is tricky because `tl.where` creates a new tensor. We can do: ```python A = tl.load(...) for i in range(1, C): row_i = A[i, :] rows_left = A[:, :i] update = tl.sum(row_i[:, None] * rows_left, axis=0) # (i,) # Update A[i, :i] mask = (tl.arange(0, C) == i)[:, None] & (tl.arange(0, C) < i)[None, :] A = tl.where(mask, A + update[None, :], A) ``` This should work. The mask selects row i and columns < i. We add update broadcasted. Wait, `tl.sum(row_i[:, None] * rows_left, axis=0)` sums over axis 0 which is the first dim of rows_left (C). row_i is (C,), rows_left is (C, i), product is (C, i), sum over axis 0 gives (i,). Correct. Then store A back. But loading full A (64x64 = 4KB) per block is fine. With 512 blocks, each loads 4KB. We use one block per (B,H,N) matrix. Actually 64x64 fp32 = 16KB. 512*16KB = 8MB total. The default shared memory per SM might be 164KB or 228KB. With one block per (B,H) and full S=64KB, plus q, k, u, w, Aqk tiles, it's tight but possible. Actually, I can avoid storing Aqk in shared memory by computing it on the fly? No, Aqk @ v_i needs Aqk. Alternatively, I can compute the recurrence without materializing full Aqk by iterating over j (columns) and accumulating. But that's slow. Hmm. Let me think about a single kernel that does intra + inter chunk. Single kernel per (B,H,V_tile): - Outer loop over chunks n - For each chunk: - Load q, k, v_tile, g, beta - Compute g_cumsum - Compute A_kk (C,C) in shared - Apply Woodbury - Compute w (C,K) in shared - Compute u_tile (C,V_tile) in shared - Compute Aqk (C,C) in shared (or reuse A_kk memory) - Compute v_i_tile = u_tile - w @ S_tile - Compute o_i_tile = (q*exp_g) @ S_tile + Aqk @ v_i_tile - Update S_tile - Write o_i_tile With V_tile=32, S_tile=16KB, u_tile=8KB, v_tile=8KB, o_tile=8KB, A=16KB, w=32KB, q=16KB, k=16KB, g=32KB, beta=0.1KB. Total ~130KB. Good. But Aqk can reuse A's memory. v_tile can be loaded as bf16 and converted. o_tile can be written directly. We also need workspace for computing A_kk. We can compute it using registers without storing the full CxCxK intermediate. Since A_kk = (k * exp(g)) @ (k * exp(-g)).T, we can do this as a matrix multiply using Triton's dot. But Triton's dot tiles by default. We can compute A_kk in shared memory or registers. Actually, with C=64, K=128, we can compute A_kk as: - Load k_tile (C, K) and exp_g, exp_neg_g - Compute k_pos = k * exp_g, k_neg = k * exp_neg_g - A_kk = k_pos @ k_neg.T This is a (64,128) @ (128,64) GEMM, yielding (64,64). Triton can do this with one block if we have enough registers/shared memory. The intermediate k_pos, k_neg need 2 * 64*128*4 = 64KB in fp32 or 32KB in bf16. We can keep them in bf16/fp32 and let Triton accumulate in fp32. But we also need q*exp_g for Aqk and w = A @ k_pos. So we need q*exp_g too. That's another 32KB. This is getting big. Maybe process K in tiles. For K=128, tile K into 2 tiles of 64. Then: - For each K tile: - Load k_tile, g_tile - Compute partial A_kk += (k * exp_g)_tile @ (k * exp(-g))_tile.T - For Aqk: partial Aqk += (q * exp_g)_tile @ (k * exp(-g))_tile.T - For w: partial w += A @ (k * exp_g)_tile (but A is not ready until A_kk is fully computed) So A_kk and Aqk can be computed with K tiled, then w and u. +"""KDA forward (chunk form) with custom Triton kernel.
+
+Hybrid implementation:
+  - Batched GEMMs compute A_kk, Aqk, w, u.
+  - A Triton kernel applies the in-chunk Woodbury correction to A.
+  - The inter-chunk recurrence is a Python loop over chunks using batched GEMMs.
+
+This avoids calling FLA's existing KDA implementation while still using a real
+custom kernel for the non-GEMM recurrence step.
+"""
+from __future__ import annotations
+
+import torch
+import torch.nn as nn
+import triton
+import triton.language as tl
+
+
+@triton.jit
+def _woodbury_kernel(
+    A_ptr,
+    stride_b: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_h: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_n: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_i: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_j: tl.constexpr,
+    BT: tl.constexpr,
+):
+    """Apply the causal Woodbury update to A (B, H, N, BT, BT).
+
+    For each 64x64 matrix, initial A is strictly lower triangular (diag zero).
+    For i = 1 .. BT-1:
+        A[i, :i] += sum_m A[i, m] * A[m, :i]
+    This is done fully in registers/shared memory for one matrix per block.
+    """
+    pid_b = tl.program_id(0)
+    pid_h = tl.program_id(1)
+    pid_n = tl.program_id(2)
+
+    base = (
+        A_ptr
+        + pid_b * stride_b
+        + pid_h * stride_h
+        + pid_n * stride_n
+    )
+
+    offs_i = tl.arange(0, BT)
+    offs_j = tl.arange(0, BT)
+    A = tl.load(base + offs_i[:, None] * stride_i + offs_j[None, :] * stride_j)
+
+    for i in range(1, BT):
+        row_i = A[i, :]  # (BT,)
+        rows_left = A[:, :i]  # (BT, i)
+        update = tl.sum(row_i[:, None] * rows_left, axis=0)  # (i,)
+        mask = (offs_i == i)[:, None] & (offs_j < i)[None, :]
+        A = tl.where(mask, A + update[None, :], A)
+
+    tl.store(base + offs_i[:, None] * stride_i + offs_j[None, :] * stride_j, A)
+
+
+def _woodbury(A: torch.Tensor) -> torch.Tensor:
+    """In-place Woodbury update on A (B, H, N, BT, BT)."""
+    B, H, N, BT, _ = A.shape
+    grid = (B, H, N)
+    _woodbury_kernel[grid](
+        A,
+        A.stride(0),
+        A.stride(1),
+        A.stride(2),
+        A.stride(3),
+        A.stride(4),
+        BT=BT,
+    )
+    return A
+
+
+def _chunk_kda_forward(
+    q: torch.Tensor,
+    k: torch.Tensor,
+    v: torch.Tensor,
+    g: torch.Tensor,
+    beta: torch.Tensor,
+    scale: float,
+    chunk_size: int = 64,
+) -> torch.Tensor:
+    dtype = v.dtype
+    B, T, H, K = q.shape
+    V = v.shape[-1]
+    BT = chunk_size
+    NT = T // BT
+
+    q, k, v, g, beta = (x.to(torch.float32) for x in (q, k, v, g, beta))
+    q = q * scale
+
+    # (B, T, H, D) -> (B, H, N, C, D)
+    q = q.view(B, NT, BT, H, K).permute(0, 3, 1, 2, 4).contiguous()
+    k = k.view(B, NT, BT, H, K).permute(0, 3, 1, 2, 4).contiguous()
+    v = v.view(B, NT, BT, H, V).permute(0, 3, 1, 2, 4).contiguous()
+    g = g.view(B, NT, BT, H, K).permute(0, 3, 1, 2, 4).contiguous()
+    beta = beta.view(B, NT, BT, H).permute(0, 3, 1, 2).contiguous()
+
+    g = g.cumsum(-2)
+    exp_g = g.exp()
+    exp_neg_g = (-g).exp()
+
+    # ---- Intra-chunk A_kk (causal, diag masked) ----
+    # A_kk[i, j] = -beta[j] * sum_d k[i,d] * k[j,d] * exp(g[i,d] - g[j,d]) for i > j
+    #            = -beta[j] * (k * exp(g)) @ (k * exp(-g)).T
+    k_pos = k * exp_g  # (B,H,N,C,K)
+    k_neg = k * exp_neg_g  # (B,H,N,C,K)
+    A = torch.matmul(k_pos, k_neg.transpose(-2, -1))  # (B,H,N,C,C)
+    # Apply causal mask (strict lower triangular, diag zero)
+    mask_upper = torch.triu(torch.ones(BT, BT, dtype=torch.bool, device=q.device), diagonal=0)
+    A = -A.masked_fill(mask_upper, 0.0)
+
+    # Woodbury update
+    _woodbury(A)
+
+    # Final scaling: A = (A + I) * beta[..., None, :]
+    A = (A + torch.eye(BT, dtype=torch.float32, device=q.device)) * beta[..., None, :]
+
+    # w = A @ (exp(g) * k), u = A @ v
+    w = torch.matmul(A, k_pos)  # (B,H,N,C,K)
+    u = torch.matmul(A, v)  # (B,H,N,C,V)
+
+    # ---- Inter-chunk recurrence ----
+    S = q.new_zeros(B, H, K, V)
+    o = torch.zeros_like(v)
+    mask_strict_upper = torch.triu(torch.ones(BT, BT, dtype=torch.bool, device=q.device), diagonal=1)
+
+    # Precompute Aqk for all chunks: (q * exp(g)) @ (k * exp(-g)).T
+    q_pos = q * exp_g
+    Aqk = torch.matmul(q_pos, k_neg.transpose(-2, -1))
+    Aqk = Aqk.masked_fill(mask_strict_upper, 0.0)
+
+    for i in range(NT):
+        q_i = q[:, :, i]
+        k_i = k[:, :, i]
+        u_i = u[:, :, i]
+        g_i = g[:, :, i]
+        w_i = w[:, :, i]
+        exp_g_i = exp_g[:, :, i]
+        Aqk_i = Aqk[:, :, i]
+
+        v_i = u_i - torch.matmul(w_i, S)
+        o[:, :, i] = torch.matmul(q_i * exp_g_i, S) + torch.matmul(Aqk_i, v_i)
+
+        # S = S * exp(g_i[:, :, -1]).reshape(...)
+        S = S * g_i[:, :, -1].exp().unsqueeze(-1)
+        # S += (exp(g_i[:,:,-1:] - g_i) * k_i).transpose @ v_i
+        kg = (g_i[:, :, -1:].exp() * exp_neg_g[:, :, i]) * k_i  # = exp(g_last - g) * k
+        S = S + torch.matmul(kg.transpose(-2, -1), v_i)
+
+    o = o.permute(0, 2, 3, 1, 4).contiguous().view(B, T, H, V)
+    return o.to(dtype)
+
+
+class Model(nn.Module):
+    """KDA forward (chunk form). No learned parameters; all inputs are activations."""
+
+    def __init__(self, B: int, T: int, H: int, K: int, V: int, chunk_size: int = 64):
+        super().__init__()
+        self.B, self.T, self.H, self.K, self.V = B, T, H, K, V
+        self.chunk_size = chunk_size
+        self.scale = float(K) ** -0.5
+        self.register_buffer("_dummy", torch.zeros(1), persistent=False)
+
+    def forward(
+        self,
+        q: torch.Tensor,
+        k: torch.Tensor,
+        v: torch.Tensor,
+        g: torch.Tensor,
+        beta: torch.Tensor,
+    ) -> torch.Tensor:
+        return _chunk_kda_forward(q, k, v, g, beta, scale=self.scale, chunk_size=self.chunk_size)
+
+
+# Module-level shape shims (overridden by check.py / benchmark.py per shape).
+B = 2
+T = 1024
+H = 8
+K = 128
+V = 128
+CHUNK_SIZ

import torch
from einops import rearrange
import reference

B,T,H,K,V,CHUNK_SIZE = 2,1024,8,128,128,64
device='cuda:0'
for k,v in {'B':B,'T':T,'H':H,'K':K,'V':V,'CHUNK_SIZE':CHUNK_SIZE}.items():
    setattr(reference, k, v)

torch.manual_seed(42)
torch.cuda.manual_seed_all(42)
q,k,v,g,beta = [t.to(device) if hasattr(t,'to') else t for t in reference.get_inputs()]
q = q*2; k=k*2; v=v*2
scale = K**-0.5

# Run reference up to chunk 1
import torch.nn as nn
q32,k32,v32,g32,beta32 = (x.to(torch.float32) for x in (q,k,v,g,beta))
q32 = q32 * scale
q32 = rearrange(q32, 'b (n c) h d -> b h n c d', c=CHUNK_SIZE)
k32 = rearrange(k32, 'b (n c) h d -> b h n c d', c=CHUNK_SIZE)
v32 = rearrange(v32, 'b (n c) h d -> b h n c d', c=CHUNK_SIZE)
g32 = rearrange(g32, 'b (n c) h d -> b h n c d', c=CHUNK_SIZE)
beta32 = rearrange(beta32, 'b (n c) h -> b h n c', c=CHUNK_SIZE)
g32 = g32.cumsum(-2)
exp_g = g32.exp()

S = q32.new_zeros(B,H,K,V)
for i in range(2):
    q_i = q32[:,:,i]
    k_i = k32[:,:,i]
    g_i = g32[:,:,i]
    exp_g_i = exp_g[:,:,i]
    v_i = v32[:,:,i]
    # Just do simple linear attention update for reference
    S = S * g_i[:,:,-1].exp().unsqueeze(-1)
    S = S + (k_i.transpose(-2,-1) @ (exp_g_i * v_i))  # standard linear attention
    print(f'chunk {i} S norm', S.norm().item())

# Now compute my solution's S update logic
S2 = q32.new_zeros(B,H,K,V)
for i in range(2):
    q_i = q32[:,:,i]
    k_i = k32[:,:,i]
    g_i = g32[:,:,i]
    exp_g_i = exp_g[:,:,i]
    beta_i = beta32[:,:,i]
    v_i = v32[:,:,i]
    
    # A_kk
    k_pos = k_i * exp_g_i
    k_neg = k_i * (-g_i).exp()
    A = -beta_i.unsqueeze(-2) * (k_pos @ k_neg.transpose(-2,-1))
    mask = torch.triu(torch.ones(CHUNK_SIZE,CHUNK_SIZE,device=device,dtype=torch.bool),diagonal=0)
    A = A.masked_fill(mask, 0.0)
    
    # Woodbury
    for j in range(1, CHUNK_SIZE):
        A[..., j, :j] = A[..., j, :j] + (A[..., j, :, None] * A[..., :, :j]).sum(-2)
    A = (A + torch.eye(CHUNK_SIZE,device=device)) * beta_i.unsqueeze(-2)
    
    u = A @ v_i
    w = A @ k_pos
    
    # Aqk
    q_pos = q_i * exp_g_i
    Aqk = q_pos @ k_neg.transpose(-2,-1)
    mask2 = torch.triu(torch.ones(CHUNK_SIZE,CHUNK_SIZE,device=device,dtype=torch.bool),diagonal=1)
    Aqk = Aqk.masked_fill(mask2, 0.0)
    
    v_i2 = u - w @ S2
    kg = (g_i[:,:,-1:].exp() * (-g_i).exp()) * k_i
    S2 = S2 * g_i[:,:,-1].exp().unsqueeze(-1)
    S2 = S2 + kg.transpose(-2,-1) @ v_i2
    print(f'chunk {i} S2 norm', S2.norm().item())

print('S diff norm', (S-S2).norm().item())
"

reasoning (2408 chars)
Interesting! Even my vectorized implementation has max diff 0.075 with large scaling, which exceeds 0.05. So there's a fundamental numerical difference between the reference naive implementation and the vectorized/batched-GEMM implementation. This is likely due to summation order differences in the GEMMs vs the einsum loops. For nominal, max diff was 0.0026 (within tolerance). For large_qkv, 0.075 (exceeds). The reference uses einsum over K dimension in a specific order, while batched GEMM uses different tiling/summation. This means my batched-GEMM approach might not achieve the required tolerance for large_qkv. I need to match the reference's numerical behavior more closely. How can I match the reference? The reference computes: ```python A[..., i] = torch.einsum("... c d, ... d -> ... c", k * (g - g_i).exp(), k_i) ``` This is equivalent to sum_d k[c,d] * k[i,d] * exp(g[c,d] - g[i,d]) for each c, with a fixed i. The summation over d is done in a specific order (d=0,1,...,K-1). In my batched GEMM: A_kk = (k * exp_g) @ (k * exp_neg_g).T This computes sum_d (k[c,d]*exp_g[c,d]) * (k[i,d]*exp_neg_g[i,d]). The summation order is determined by cuBLAS, which splits K into tiles and accumulates in a different order. For bf16/fp32 mixed precision, summation order can matter. But here all intermediate are fp32. Still, the order of additions can affect the result slightly, and with large scaling and long recurrence, errors amplify. Wait, but the reference uses fp32 too. The difference between einsum order and GEMM order in fp32 is usually small (sub-ULP), not 0.075. Unless K=128 and values ~0.2, the difference could be ~1e-5. But 0.075 is large. Actually, the issue might be that the reference computes `k * (g - g_i).exp()` first, which is k * exp(g - g_i). This involves computing exp(g - g_i) for each pair (c, i). My approach computes exp(g) and exp(-g) separately and multiplies. Mathematically equivalent but numerically: - Reference: exp(g_c - g_i) computed directly, then multiplied by k_c * k_i. - Mine: exp(g_c) * exp(-g_i) = exp(g_c - g_i) but computed as two exp operations and a multiplication. For small g, exp(g_c - g_i) vs exp(g_c)*exp(-g_i) might differ slightly due to rounding. But g values are small (~-0.05), so exp is close to 1. The difference should be tiny. Hmm. Let me test this directly: compare reference's A_kk to my batched GEMM A_kk for large scaling.

import torch
from einops import rearrange

B,T,H,K,V,CHUNK_SIZE = 2,128,8,128,128,64
device='cuda:0'
torch.manual_seed(42)
torch.cuda.manual_seed_all(42)
q = torch.randn(B, T, H, K, dtype=torch.bfloat16, device=device) * 0.1 * 2.0
k = torch.randn(B, T, H, K, dtype=torch.bfloat16, device=device) * 0.1 * 2.0
v = torch.randn(B, T, H, V, dtype=torch.bfloat16, device=device) * 0.1 * 2.0
g = (torch.randn(B, T, H, K, dtype=torch.float32, device=device) * 0.1 - 0.05)
beta = torch.sigmoid(torch.randn(B, T, H, dtype=torch.bfloat16, device=device))

q,k,v,g,beta = (x.to(torch.float32) for x in (q,k,v,g,beta))
q = rearrange(q, 'b (n c) h d -> b h n c d', c=CHUNK_SIZE)
k = rearrange(k, 'b (n c) h d -> b h n c d', c=CHUNK_SIZE)
g = rearrange(g, 'b (n c) h d -> b h n c d', c=CHUNK_SIZE)
beta = rearrange(beta, 'b (n c) h -> b h n c', c=CHUNK_SIZE)
g = g.cumsum(-2)
exp_g = g.exp()
exp_neg_g = (-g).exp()

# Reference A_kk for chunk 0
BT = CHUNK_SIZE
mask_diag_upper = torch.triu(torch.ones(BT, BT, dtype=torch.bool, device=device), diagonal=0)
A_ref = torch.zeros(B,H,1,BT,BT, dtype=torch.float32, device=device)
ki = k[:,:,0]
gi = g[:,:,0]
for i in range(BT):
    k_i = ki[..., i, :]
    g_i = gi[..., i:i + 1, :]
    A_ref[..., i] = torch.einsum('... c d, ... d -> ... c', ki * (gi - g_i).exp(), k_i)
A_ref = A_ref * beta[:,:,0:1,:,None]
A_ref = -A_ref.masked_fill(mask_diag_upper, 0)

# My A_kk
k_pos = ki * exp_g[:,:,0]
k_neg = ki * exp_neg_g[:,:,0]
A_my = -beta[:,:,0:1,:,None] * (k_pos @ k_neg.transpose(-2,-1))
A_my = A_my.masked_fill(mask_diag_upper, 0)

diff = (A_ref - A_my).abs()
print('A_kk max diff', diff.max().item())
print('A_kk mean diff', diff.mean().item())

import solution
from shapes import SHAPES

shape = SHAPES[1]
B,T,H,K,V = shape['B'], shape['T'], shape['H'], shape['K'], shape['V']

Kernel design: - One block per (B, H, V_tile) - Loop over chunks n = 0..N-1 - Keep S_tile (K, V_tile) in shared memory - Precompute all needed per-chunk tensors in PyTorch and load them in the kernel: - qg = q * exp_g (B,H,N,C,K) -> for qg @ S - u (B,H,N,C,V) -> for v_i - w (B,H,N,C,K) -> for w @ S - Aqk (B,H,N,C,C) -> for Aqk @ v_i - kg = (g_last - g).exp() * k (B,H,N,C,K) -> for S update - g_last_exp = exp(g[:,:,:,-1]) (B,H,N,K) -> for S scaling - Compute v_i_tile = u_tile - w @ S_tile - o_i_tile = qg @ S_tile + Aqk @ v_i_tile - S_tile = S_tile * g_last_exp[..., None] + kg.T @ v_i_tile Wait, but u_tile depends on V tile. We need to load u[:,:,:,v_start:v_end] each chunk. Similarly v_i_tile and o_i_tile. Actually, maybe it's better to process full V in one block. These are small but with batch=16 (B*H) and 2 V tiles, total work is decent. But inside the kernel, each block does sequential chunks. With C=64, K=128, V_tile=64, the block can do these GEMMs efficiently. But Triton's `tl.dot` works on tiles. With K=128 and V_tile=64, we might tile further, e.g., block size 64x64. +import torch
+import triton
+import triton.language as tl
+
+
+@triton.jit
+def _recurrent_kernel(
+    qg_ptr,
+    u_ptr,
+    w_ptr,
+    Aqk_ptr,
+    kg_ptr,
+    gscale_ptr,
+    o_ptr,
+    B: tl.constexpr,
+    H: tl.constexpr,
+    N: tl.constexpr,
+    C: tl.constexpr,
+    K: tl.constexpr,
+    V: tl.constexpr,
+    V_TILE: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_qgb: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_qgh: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_qgn: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_qgc: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_qgk: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_ub: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_uh: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_un: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_uc: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_uv: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_wb: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_wh: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_wn: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_wc: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_wk: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_Aqkb: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_Aqkh: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_Aqkn: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_Aqki: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_Aqkj: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_kgb: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_kgh: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_kgn: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_kgc: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_kgk: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_gsb: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_gsh: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_gsn: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_gsk: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_ob: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_oh: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_on: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_oc: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_ov: tl.constexpr,
+):
+    pid_b = tl.program_id(0)
+    pid_h = tl.program_program_id(1)
+    pid_vtile = tl.program_id(2)
+    v_start = pid_vtile * V_TILE
+
+    # S tile in shared memory / registers
+    offs_k = tl.arange(0, K)
+    offs_v = tl.arange(0, V_TILE) + v_start
+    S = tl.zeros((K, V_TILE), dtype=tl.float32)
+
+    offs_c = tl.arange(0, C)
+
+    for n in range(N):
+        # Pointers for this chunk
+        qg_b = qg_ptr + pid_b * stride_qgb + pid_h * stride_qgh + n * stride_qgn
+        u_b = u_ptr + pid_b * stride_ub + pid_h * stride_uh + n * stride_un
+        w_b = w_ptr + pid_b * stride_wb + pid_h * stride_wh + n * stride_wn
+        Aqk_b = Aqk_ptr + pid_b * stride_Aqkb + pid_h * stride_Aqkh + n * stride_Aqkn
+        kg_b = kg_ptr + pid_b * stride_kgb + pid_h * stride_kgh + n * stride_kgn
+        gs_b = gscale_ptr + pid_b * stride_gsb + pid_h * stride_gsh + n * stride_gsn
+        o_b = o_ptr + pid_b * stride_ob + pid_h * stride_oh + n * stride_on
+
+        # Load u tile: (C, V_TILE)
+        u = tl.load(u_b + offs_c[:, None] * stride_uc + offs_v[None, :] * stride_uv)
+
+        # Compute w @ S -> v_w = (C, V_TILE)
+        w = tl.load(w_b + offs_c[:, None] * stride_wc + offs_k[None, :] * stride_wk)
+        v_w = tl.dot(w, S)
+        v_i = u - v_w
+
+        # Compute o = qg @ S + Aqk @ v_i
+        qg = tl.load(qg_b + offs_c[:, None] * stride_qgc + offs_k[None, :] * stride_qgk)
+        o = tl.dot(qg, S)
+
+        Aqk = tl.load(Aqk_b + offs_c[:, None] * stride_Aqki + offs_c[None, :] * stride_Aqkj)
+        o = o + tl.dot(Aqk, v_i)
+        tl.store(o_b + offs_c[:, None] * stride_oc + offs_v[None, :] * stride_ov, o.to(tl.bfloat16))
+
+        # Update S: S = S * gscale[:, None] + kg.T @ v_i
+        gscale = tl.load(gs_b + offs_k * stride_gsk)  # (K,)
+        S = S * gscale[:, None]
+
+        kg = tl.load(kg_b + offs_c[:, None] * stride_kgc + offs_k[None, :] * stride_kgk)
+        # kg is (C, K), need (K, C) for dot with (C, V_TILE)
+        S = S + tl.dot(kg.trans(), v_i)
+
+
+def recurrent_triton(qg, u, w, Aqk, kg, gscale, o):
+    B, H, N, C, K = qg.shape
+    V = o.shape[-1]
+    V_TILE = 64
+    num_v_tiles = V // V_TILE
+    grid = (B, H, num_v_tiles)
+    _recurrent_kernel[grid](
+        qg, u, w, Aqk, kg, gscale, o,
+        B=B, H=H, N=N, C=C, K=K, V=V, V_TILE=V_TILE,
+        stride_qgb=qg.stride(0), stride_qgh=qg.stride(1), stride_qgn=qg.stride(2), stride_qgc=qg.stride(3), stride_qgk=qg.stride(4),
+        stride_ub=u.stride(0), stride_uh=u.stride(1), stride_un=u.stride(2), stride_uc=u.stride(3), stride_uv=u.stride(4),
+        stride_wb=w.stride(0), stride_wh=w.stride(1), stride_wn=w.stride(2), stride_wc=w.stride(3), stride_wk=w.stride(4),
+        stride_Aqkb=Aqk.stride(0), stride_Aqkh=Aqk.stride(1), stride_Aqkn=Aqk.stride(2), stride_Aqki=Aqk.stride(3), stride_Aqkj=Aqk.stride(4),
+        stride_kgb=kg.stride(0), stride_kgh=kg.stride(1), stride_kgn=kg.stride(2), stride_kgc=kg.stride(3), stride_kgk=kg.stride(4),
+        stride_gsb=gscale.stride(0), stride_gsh=gscale.stride(1), stride_gsn=gscale.stride(2), stride_gsk=gscale.stride(3),
+        stride_ob=o.stride(0), stride_oh=o.stride(1), stride_on=o.stride(2), stride_oc=o.stride(3), stride_ov=o.stride(4),
+    )
+    return o
+
+
+if __name__ == "__main__":
+    B,H,N,C,K,V = 2,4,2,64,128,128
+    device='cuda:0'
+    qg = torch.randn(B,H,N,C,K, dtype=torch.float32, device=device)
+    u = torch.randn(B,H,N,C,V, dtype=torch.float32, device=device)
+    w = torch.randn(B,H,N,C,K, dtype=torch.float32, device=device)
+    Aqk = torch.randn(B,H,N,C,C, dtype=torch.float32, device=device)
+    kg = torch.randn(B,H,N,C,K, dtype=torch.float32, device=device)
+    gscale = torch.randn(B,H,N,K, dtype=torch.float32, device=device)
+    o = torch.empty(B,H,N,C,V, dtype=torch.bfloat16, device=device)
+    recurrent_triton(qg, u, w, Aqk, kg, gscale, o)
+    print(o.shape, o.dtype)
args

+def recurrent_pytorch(qg, u, w, Aqk, kg, gscale):
+    B, H, N, C, K = qg.shape
+    V = u.shape[-1]
+    S = qg.new_zeros(B, H, K, V)
+    o = qg.new_empty(B, H, N, C, V, dtype=torch.bfloat16)
+    for n in range(N):
+        v_i = u[:, :, n] - w[:, :, n] @ S
+        o[:, :, n] = (qg[:, :, n] @ S + Aqk[:, :, n] @ v_i).to(torch.bfloat16)
+        S = S * gscale[:, :, n].unsqueeze(-1) + kg[:, :, n].transpose(-2, -1) @ v_i
+    return o

in 105482out 0cache_r 0cache_w 0
tool
stdout (7238 chars) — TRUNCATED
1	"""KDA forward (chunk form) with custom Triton kernel.
2	
3	Hybrid implementation:
4	  - Batched GEMMs compute A_kk, Aqk, w, u.
5	  - A Triton kernel applies the in-chunk Woodbury correction to A.
6	  - The inter-chunk recurrence is a Python loop over chunks using batched GEMMs.
7	
8	This avoids calling FLA's existing KDA implementation while still using a real
9	custom kernel for the non-GEMM recurrence step.
10	"""
11	from __future__ import annotations
12	
13	import torch
14	import torch.nn as nn
15	import triton
16	import triton.language as tl
17	
18	
19	@triton.jit
20	def _woodbury_kernel(
21	    A_ptr,
22	    stride_b: tl.constexpr,
23	    stride_h: tl.constexpr,
24	    stride_n: tl.constexpr,
25	    stride_i: tl.constexpr,
26	    stride_j: tl.constexpr,
27	    BT: tl.constexpr,
28	):
29	    """Apply the causal Woodbury update to A (B, H, N, BT, BT).
30	
31	    For each 64x64 matrix, initial A is strictly lower triangular (diag zero).
32	    For i = 1 .. BT-1:
33	        A[i, :i] += sum_m A[i, m] * A[m, :i]
34	    This is done fully in registers/shared memory for one matrix per block.
35	    """
36	    pid_b = tl.program_id(0)
37	    pid_h = tl.program_id(1)
38	    pid_n = tl.program_id(2)
39	
40	    base = (
41	        A_ptr
42	        + pid_b * stride_b
43	        + pid_h * stride_h
44	        + pid_n * stride_n
45	    )
46	
47	    offs_i = tl.arange(0, BT)
48	    offs_j = tl.arange(0, BT)
49	    A = tl.load(base + offs_i[:, None] * stride_i + offs_j[None, :] * strid

 import torch.nn as nn
 import triton
 import triton.language as tl
+
+
+@triton.jit
+def _recurrent_kernel(
+    qg_ptr,
+    u_ptr,
+    w_ptr,
+    Aqk_ptr,
+    kg_ptr,
+    gscale_ptr,
+    o_ptr,
+    B: tl.constexpr,
+    H: tl.constexpr,
+    N: tl.constexpr,
+    C: tl.constexpr,
+    K: tl.constexpr,
+    V: tl.constexpr,
+    V_TILE: tl.constexpr,
+    BLOCK_K: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_qgb: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_qgh: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_qgn: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_qgc: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_qgk: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_ub: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_uh: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_un: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_uc: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_uv: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_wb: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_wh: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_wn: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_wc: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_wk: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_Aqkb: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_Aqkh: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_Aqkn: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_Aqki: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_Aqkj: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_kgb: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_kgh: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_kgn: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_kgc: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_kgk: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_gsb: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_gsh: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_gsn: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_gsk: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_ob: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_oh: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_on: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_oc: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_ov: tl.constexpr,
+):
+    """Inter-chunk recurrence for KDA.
+
+    One block handles one (batch, head, V-tile) and loops over chunks.
+    State tiles S0/S1 are persistent in shared memory / registers.
+    """
+    pid_b = tl.program_id(0)
+    pid_h = tl.program_id(1)
+    pid_vtile = tl.program_id(2)
+    v_start = pid_vtile * V_TILE
+
+    offs_c = tl.arange(0, C)
+    offs_v = tl.arange(0, V_TILE) + v_start
+    offs_k0 = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_K)
+    offs_k1 = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_K) + BLOCK_K
+
+    # Persistent state for K = 2 * BLOCK_K
+    S0 = tl.zeros((BLOCK_K, V_TILE), dtype=tl.float32)
+    S1 = tl.zeros((BLOCK_K, V_TILE), dtype=tl.float32)
+
+    for n in range(N):
+        qg_b = qg_ptr + pid_b * stride_qgb + pid_h * stride_qgh + n * stride_qgn
+        u_b = u_ptr + pid_b * stride_ub + pid_h * stride_uh + n * stride_un
+        w_b = w_ptr + pid_b * stride_wb + pid_h * stride_wh + n * stride_wn
+        Aqk_b = Aqk_ptr + pid_b * stride_Aqkb + pid_h * stride_Aqkh + n * stride_Aqkn
+        kg_b = kg_ptr + pid_b * stride_kgb + pid_h * stride_kgh + n * stride_kgn
+        gs_b = gscale_ptr + pid_b * stride_gsb + pid_h * stride_gsh + n * stride_gsn
+        o_b = o_ptr + pid_b * stride_ob + pid_h * stride_oh + n * stride_on
+
+        u = tl.load(u_b + offs_c[:, None] * stride_uc + offs_v[None, :] * stride_uv)
+
+        w0 = tl.load(w_b + offs_c[:, None] * stride_wc + offs_k0[None, :] * stride_wk)
+        w1 = tl.load(w_b + offs_c[:, None] * stride_wc + offs_k1[None, :] * stride_wk)
+        v_i = u - tl.dot(w0, S0) - tl.dot(w1, S1)
+
+        qg0 = tl.load(qg_b + offs_c[:, None] * stride_qgc + offs_k0[None, :] * stride_qgk)
+        qg1 = tl.load(qg_b + offs_c[:, None] * stride_qgc + offs_k1[None, :] * stride_qgk)
+        o = tl.dot(qg0, S0) + tl.dot(qg1, S1)
+
+        Aqk = tl.load(Aqk_b + offs_c[:, None] * stride_Aqki + offs_c[None, :] * stride_Aqkj)
+        o = o + tl.dot(Aqk, v_i)
+        tl.store(o_b + offs_c[:, None] * stride_oc + offs_v[None, :] * stride_ov, o.to(tl.bfloat16))
+
+        gscale0 = tl.load(gs_b + offs_k0 * stride_gsk)
+        gscale1 = tl.load(gs_b + offs_k1 * stride_gsk)
+        S0 = S0 * gscale0[:, None]
+        S1 = S1 * gscale1[:, None]
+
+        kg0 = tl.load(kg_b + offs_k0[:, None] * stride_kgk + offs_c[None, :] * stride_kgc)
+        kg1 = tl.load(kg_b + offs_k1[:, None] * stride_kgk + offs_c[None, :] * stride_kgc)
+        S0 = S0 + tl.dot(kg0, v_i)
+        S1 = S1 + tl.dot(kg1, v_i)
+
+
+def _recurrent_triton(qg, u, w, Aqk, kg, gscale, o):
+    B, H, N, C, K = qg.shape
+    V = o.shape[-1]
+    V_TILE = 16
+    BLOCK_K = 64
+    num_v_tiles = V // V_TILE
+    grid = (B, H, num_v_tiles)
+    _recurrent_kernel[grid](
+        qg, u, w, Aqk, kg, gscale, o,
+        B=B, H=H, N=N, C=C, K=K, V=V, V_TILE=V_TILE, BLOCK_K=BLOCK_K,
+        stride_qgb=qg.stride(0), stride_qgh=qg.stride(1), stride_qgn=qg.stride(2), stride_qgc=qg.stride(3), stride_qgk=qg.stride(4),
+        stride_ub=u.stride(0), stride_uh=u.stride(1), stride_un=u.stride(2), stride_uc=u.stride(3), stride_uv=u.stride(4),
+        stride_wb=w.stride(0), stride_wh=w.stride(1), stride_wn=w.stride(2), stride_wc=w.stride(3), stride_wk=w.stride(4),
+        stride_Aqkb=Aqk.stride(0), stride_Aqkh=Aqk.stride(1), stride_Aqkn=Aqk.stride(2), stride_Aqki=Aqk.stride(3), stride_Aqkj=Aqk.stride(4),
+        stride_kgb=kg.stride(0), stride_kgh=kg.stride(1), stride_kgn=kg.stride(2), stride_kgc=kg.stride(3), stride_kgk=kg.stride(4),
+        stride_gsb=gscale.stride(0), stride_gsh=gscale.stride(1), stride_gsn=gscale.stride(2), stride_gsk=gscale.stride(3),
+        stride_ob=o.stride(0), stride_oh=o.stride(1), stride_on=o.stride(2), stride_oc=o.stride(3), stride_ov=o.stride(4),
+        num_warps=8,
+        num_stages=1,
+    )
+    return o

The profiler shows: - `_recurrent_kernel`: 1.44ms total for 10 iters = 0.144ms per iter (29.94%) - `_woodbury_kernel`: 0.58ms total = 0.058ms per iter (12.15%) - Elementwise kernels: ~1.5ms total (30%+) - GEMM kernels: ~0.44ms total (9%) - Scan (cumsum): 0.1ms (2%) So the PyTorch elementwise ops and GEMMs are taking significant time. The recurrent kernel is only 30%. To improve further, I need to: 1. Fuse more elementwise ops into fewer kernels or into Triton 2. Reduce GEMM overhead 3. Possibly fuse intra-chunk computations into Triton/CUDA Actually, the biggest wins would be: - Fuse the elementwise operations (k_pos, k_neg, q_pos, gscale, kg, beta scaling, masking) into fewer kernels - Use more efficient data layout to reduce permutes/contiguous ops - Fuse the Woodbury + A computation into one kernel or into the recurrence But let me think about what's actually slow. The recurrent kernel takes 0.144ms for shape 1 (B=2,H=8,N=32). Total time 0.5ms. So other stuff is 0.356ms. For shape 1, the FLOPs are ~5.7B (estimated). At 0.5ms, that's 11.4 TFLOPS. Peak bf16 on RTX PRO 6000 is ~200 TFLOPS (maybe). So 5.7% peak. To get to 10% peak, I need ~0.28ms for shape 1. That means roughly halving the time. Where can I save? - Elementwise kernels: 30% of time. Fusing them could save maybe half. - Recurrent kernel: 30%. Could optimize by using larger V_TILE or better tiling. - GEMMs: 10%. Hard to reduce. - Woodbury: 12%. Already a custom kernel, could optimize but small. Actually, maybe I should write a single fused Triton kernel for the entire forward pass, processing chunks sequentially and doing intra + inter chunk in one block. This would eliminate most elementwise kernels and GEMM launches. But shared memory is tight. Let me think about a fully fused kernel. Fully fused kernel per (B, H, V_tile): - Loop over chunks n - Load q, k, v_tile, g, beta - Compute g_cumsum - Compute k_pos, k_neg - Compute A_kk = k_pos @ k_neg.T - Apply row beta, mask, negate - Woodbury update - Final column beta scaling: A = (A + I) * beta_col - Compute w = A @ k_pos (needed for recurrence) - Compute u_tile = A @ v_tile - Compute q_pos - Compute Aqk = q_pos @ k_neg.T, mask strict upper - Compute v_i = u_tile - w @ S_tile - Compute o = q_pos @ S_tile + Aqk @ v_i - Compute gscale, kg - Update S_tile Shared memory needed at peak: - S_tile (K, V_TILE). If V_TILE=16: 8KB - q/k/g/beta/v tiles. We can load in bf16 and convert. - A (C,C) fp32: 16KB - w (C,K) fp32: 32KB - u_tile/v_i/o_tile: 3 * 64*16*4 = 12KB - Aqk can reuse A memory - k_pos/k_neg/q_pos can be computed on the fly or reused buffers - kg/gscale computed Peak: S 8 + A/w 48 + u/v/o 12 + q/k/g buffers ~40KB + kg ~32KB = 140KB. If I use bf16 for some GEMMs, I might exceed tolerance. Better stay fp32. Another idea: the elementwise ops include creating `k_pos`, `k_neg`, `q_pos`, `exp_g`, `exp_neg_g`, `gscale`, `kg`, and various masks. Many of these are temporary and can be fused. I can write a single Triton kernel that computes all the per-chunk precomputed tensors (qg, u, w, Aqk, kg, gscale) from q, k, v, g, beta. But u and w require GEMMs, so I'd need to do GEMMs in Triton. Actually, maybe the simplest big win is to fuse the recurrence kernel with the precomputation of qg, kg, gscale, so we don't need to materialize them. But u, w, Aqk still need precomputation. Wait, I can also compute u and w in the recurrent kernel on the fly if I load v and k and A. But A is computed from k and g, which requires the Woodbury update. It's a chicken-and-egg problem. Hmm. Let me step back. The current solution gets 3% peak fraction. The benchmark says RESULT: LOW (needs >= 10%). I need a ~3x speedup. One approach: fuse the recurrence and the per-chunk precomputations into one big Triton kernel. But shared memory is too tight. In solution.py: ```python q = q.view(B, NT, BT, H, K).permute(0, 3, 1, 2, 4).contiguous() ``` This creates a contiguous tensor. The permute is necessary. But maybe I can use `einops.rearrange` or keep non-contiguous and let GEMMs handle it. Actually, `torch.matmul` on non-contiguous tensors might be slower. But maybe not. Let me see if I can reduce elementwise ops. The main elementwise ops are: - `q = q * scale` - `g = g.cumsum(-2)` - `exp_g = g.exp()` - `exp_neg_g = (-g).exp()` - `k_pos = k * exp_g` - `k_neg = k * exp_neg_g` - `A = A * beta[..., None]` - `A = -A.masked_fill(mask_upper, 0.0)` - `A = (A + I) * beta[..., None, :]` - `q_pos = q * exp_g` - `Aqk = Aqk.masked_fill(mask_strict_upper, 0.0)` - `gscale = g[:, :, :, -1].exp()` - `kg = (g[:, :, :, -1:].exp() * exp_neg_g) * k` Many of these can be fused. I can write a custom Triton kernel to compute qg, kg, gscale from q, k, g in one go. Similarly for k_pos, k_neg. Actually, let me think about the bigger picture. The recurrent kernel takes 0.144ms. The total is 0.5ms. Even if I eliminate all elementwise overhead, I'd be at ~0.35ms, which is ~16% peak fraction for shape 1. That would pass. So the main bottleneck is actually the recurrent kernel and the GEMMs, not just elementwise. Wait, recurrent is 0.144ms, GEMMs are ~0.44ms/10 = 0.044ms, elementwise ~0.15ms, Woodbury 0.058ms. import torch
import solution
from shapes import SHAPES

shape = SHAPES[1]
B,T,H,K,V = shape['B'], shape['T'], shape['H'], shape['K'], shape['V']
CS = shape['CHUNK_SIZE']
for k,v in shape.items():
    setattr(solution, k, v)

device='cuda:0'
model = solution.Model(B,T,H,K,V,CS).to(device).eval()
comp = torch.compile(model, mode='max-autotune')
torch.manual_seed(0)
inputs = [t.to(device) if hasattr(t,'to') else t for t in solution.get_inputs()]

# warmup
for _ in range(5):
    _ = comp(*inputs)
torch.cuda.synchronize()

import time
t0 = time.time()
for _ in range(100):
    _ = comp(*inputs)
torch.cuda.synchronize()
print('compiled ms', (time.time()-t0)*10)

# correctness
with torch.no_grad():
    ref = model(*inputs)
    c_out = comp(*inputs)
print('max diff', (ref-c_out).abs().max().item())

reasoning (8192 chars)
V_TILE=32 is actually slightly worse (3.68% vs 4.23%). Maybe due to register pressure or more shared memory. Let me revert to V_TILE=16. Actually, the issue might be that with V_TILE=32, the kernel is slower per block due to memory bandwidth, and the total time doesn't improve. Let me think about other optimizations. The recurrent kernel takes 0.128ms for shape 1. Woodbury 0.059ms. Total 0.187ms just for these two custom kernels. Plus memcpy and elementwise. What if I can eliminate the Woodbury kernel by doing it differently? The Woodbury update is sequential and takes 0.059ms. Not huge but 20%. What if I fuse the Woodbury update into the A_kk computation kernel? Instead of computing A_kk with GEMM, then launching Woodbury, then scaling, I could write a Triton kernel that computes A_kk, does Woodbury, and final scaling all in one. This saves the GEMM launch overhead and the Woodbury launch overhead, and avoids writing A to global memory and reading it back. The A_kk computation is (k_pos @ k_neg.T). For C=64, K=128, this is a batched GEMM. In Triton, I can compute it per (B,H,N) block with one thread block. The block does: - Load k_pos (64,128) and k_neg (64,128) - Compute A = k_pos @ k_neg.T (64,64) - Apply beta row scaling, mask, negate - Woodbury update - Final scaling - Store A But shared memory: k_pos 32KB, k_neg 32KB, A 16KB. Total 80KB. Plus beta 0.25KB. Should fit in 100KB! And we can reuse k_pos for w computation later? Actually, w = A @ k_pos, so if we keep k_pos, we can compute w in the same kernel and avoid storing A. But u = A @ v needs v. And Aqk needs q. Wait, we can compute A, w, and Aqk if we have q and k. But u needs v. So we need v too. If we load q, k, v in the kernel: - q (64,128) bf16 = 16KB - k (64,128) bf16 = 16KB - v (64,128) bf16 = 16KB - g (64,128) fp32 = 32KB - beta (64) bf16 = 0.1KB Total input buffers ~80KB. Plus A 16KB, w 32KB, u 32KB, Aqk 16KB. Total ~176KB. Over. But we can compute in stages: 1. Load g, compute exp_g, exp_neg_g 2. Load k, compute k_pos, k_neg (can reuse k buffer) 3. Compute A = k_pos @ k_neg.T 4. Apply beta, Woodbury, final scaling 5. Compute w = A @ k_pos, store w 6. Load v, compute u = A @ v, store u 7. Load q, compute q_pos, compute Aqk = q_pos @ k_neg.T, mask, store Aqk But we need to keep A around for steps 5,6,7. A is 16KB. k_neg is 32KB. k_pos can be recomputed from k and exp_g. q_pos from q and exp_g. Shared memory at peak: - g 32KB - k 16KB - exp_g (can be computed on the fly or stored) 32KB - k_pos/k_neg (32KB each, can reuse k buffer for one) - A 16KB - w 32KB - u 32KB - Aqk 16KB Peak ~160KB. Over. But if we store intermediate results (A, w, u, Aqk) back to global memory and free shared memory, we don't need to keep them all. We can do: - Stage 1: compute A, store A. Shared mem: g, k, A. ~80KB. - Stage 2: load A and k_pos, compute w, store w. Shared: A, k_pos, w. ~80KB. - Stage 3: load A and v, compute u, store u. Shared: A, v, u. ~80KB. - Stage 4: load q and k_neg, compute Aqk, store Aqk. Shared: q, k_neg, Aqk. ~64KB. Each stage fits. But this is multiple kernels or a single kernel with explicit global memory round-trips. Actually, I can write separate Triton kernels: - Kernel 1: compute A (intra-chunk). This replaces the GEMM + Woodbury + scaling. - Kernel 2: compute w from A and k_pos. - Kernel 3: compute u from A and v. - Kernel 4: compute Aqk from q_pos and k_neg. But that's still multiple kernels. The main win is fusing Woodbury with A_kk computation, avoiding a global round-trip. Actually, the current A_kk GEMM is very fast (0.026ms per call as shown in torch.compile autotune). The Woodbury is 0.059ms. So fusing them might save the 0.026ms GEMM time and the round-trip, but Woodbury still takes 0.059ms. Net save ~0.03ms? Not huge. The bigger win is optimizing the recurrent kernel. It takes 0.128ms. If I can halve it, that's 0.064ms save, which would bring total to ~0.30ms (from 0.365ms), or ~16% peak. How to optimize recurrent kernel? Options: 1. Increase V_TILE (didn't help with 32) 2. Use bf16 inputs for qg, w, kg, u, Aqk to reduce memory bandwidth 3. Use more threads/warps 4. Use tensor cores (tl.dot already uses them) For option 2: currently qg, u, w, Aqk, kg are fp32. The inputs q,k,v are bf16, but I compute qg etc. in fp32. If I store them as bf16, I halve memory traffic. But this might hurt correctness. Actually, the tolerance is 0.05. Storing qg, w, kg, Aqk, u as bf16 might be acceptable. The recurrent kernel loads them each chunk. Memory traffic is significant. Let me estimate memory traffic for recurrent kernel with V_TILE=16, N=32, B=2, H=8: Per block: N chunks * (qg 64*128*4 + w 64*128*4 + Aqk 64*64*4 + kg 64*128*4 + u 64*16*4 + gscale 128*4 + o write 64*16*2) = 32 * (32KB + 32KB + 16KB + 32KB + 4KB + 0.5KB + 2KB) = 32 * 118.5KB = 3.8MB per block Number of blocks = B*H*V_TILES = 2*8*8 = 128 Total traffic = 486MB. At 1.8TB/s, 0.27ms. But benchmark recurrent kernel is 0.128ms, so it's compute-bound or latency-bound, not memory-bound. Hmm, so reducing precision might not help much. Option 3: more threads/warps. Already using num_warps=8. Could try num_warps=16? But shared memory limit. Option 4: the `tl.dot` operations might not be using tensor cores efficiently due to small tile sizes. With BLOCK_K=64 and V_TILE=16, the dot is 64x64x16 or 64x64x64. For tensor cores, we want larger inner dimension. But 64 is OK. Actually, the recurrent kernel might be limited by the sequential loop over N=32 chunks and the small output tile per block. Each block does 32 chunks sequentially, and there's a dependency between chunks (S update). This limits parallelism. With B=2,H=8,V tiles=8, we have 128 blocks. On 188 SMs, that's <1 block per SM, so underutilization. For shape 3 (B=1,H=4,V tiles=8), only 32 blocks. Very underutilized. So the recurrent kernel is limited by lack of parallelism. With V_TILE=16, we have only 8 V tiles. Maybe use V_TILE=8 to get 16 V tiles and more blocks. But then each block does less work, which might increase overhead. Alternatively, process multiple (B,H) pairs per block? No, S is per (B,H). Actually, the fundamental issue is that the recurrence is sequential over N, and we parallelize only over (B,H,V_tile). For small B*H, we don't have enough blocks. For shape 3 (B=1,H=4), only 4 (B,H) pairs. With V tiles=8, 32 blocks. On 188 SMs, very low occupancy. To improve, I need to find more parallelism. One way: process chunks in groups where multiple blocks handle different chunk ranges of the same (B,H,V_tile), then combine. But the recurrence is sequential, so blocks for later chunks need S from earlier chunks. Not trivial. Another way: use larger V_TILE to reduce number of tiles but increase work per block. But that increases shared memory. Actually, maybe I should process full V=128 in one block with S in shared memory. S is 64KB. With V_TILE=128, each block handles one (B,H) pair. Then we have 16 blocks for shape 1, 4 blocks for shape 3. Even worse parallelism. Hmm. Wait, with V_TILE=16, blocks = B*H*8. For shape 1: 128 blocks. For shape 3: 32 blocks. The GPU has 188 SMs, but each SM can run multiple blocks. With 128 blocks, we might saturate. But the sequential N loop means each SM is busy for the whole duration. Actually, 128 blocks on 188 SMs means ~70% SM utilization if each block takes one SM. But blocks can be smaller. Triton's block has 8 warps = 256 threads. Each SM can run multiple blocks. So utilization might be OK. The real issue might be that the kernel is memory-bound or instruction-bound due to the loop. Let me try a different approach: use CUDA C++ for the recurrent kernel with explicit shared memory management and possibly better parallelism. Actually, before going to CUDA, let me try one more Triton optimization: use V_TILE=16 but process two V tiles per block? No, that doubles work. Or, use a 2D grid: (B*H, V_tile) with more threads per block. Already doing that. Another idea: fuse the recurrent kernel with output writing to avoid separate kernels. It already writes output. Hmm.
